<h1 id="welcome-to-llamaindex">Welcome to LlamaIndex 🦙 !<a class="headerlink" href="#welcome-to-llamaindex" title="Permanent link">#</a></h1>
<p>LlamaIndex is a framework for building context-augmented generative AI applications with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Large_language_model">LLMs</a> including <a href="./understanding/agent/basic_agent/">agents</a> and <a href="./understanding/workflows/">workflows</a>.</p>
<div class="grid cards">
<ul>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#introduction">Introduction</a></span></p>
<p>What is context augmentation? What are agents and workflows? How does LlamaIndex help build them?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#use-cases">Use cases</a></span></p>
<p>What kind of apps can you build with LlamaIndex? Who should use it?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#getting-started">Getting started</a></span></p>
<p>Get started in Python or TypeScript in just 5 lines of code!</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#llamacloud">LlamaCloud</a></span></p>
<p>Managed services for LlamaIndex including <a href="https://docs.cloud.llamaindex.ai/llamaparse/getting_started">LlamaParse</a>, the world's best document parser.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#community">Community</a></span></p>
<p>Get help and meet collaborators on Discord, Twitter, LinkedIn, and learn how to contribute to the project.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-size: 200%"><a href="#related-projects">Related projects</a></span></p>
<p>Check out our library of connectors, readers, and other integrations at <a href="https://llamahub.ai">LlamaHub</a> as well as demos and starter apps like <a href="https://www.npmjs.com/package/create-llama">create-llama</a>.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2 id="introduction">Introduction<a class="headerlink" href="#introduction" title="Permanent link">#</a></h2>
<h3 id="what-is-context-augmentation">What is context augmentation?<a class="headerlink" href="#what-is-context-augmentation" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>LLMs offer a natural language interface between humans and data. LLMs come pre-trained on huge amounts of publicly available data, but they are not trained on <strong>your</strong> data. Your data may be private or specific to the problem you're trying to solve. It's behind APIs, in SQL databases, or trapped in PDFs and slide decks.</p>
<p>Context augmentation makes your data available to the LLM to solve the problem at hand. LlamaIndex provides the tools to build any of context-augmentation use case, from prototype to production. Our tools allow you to ingest, parse, index and process your data and quickly implement complex query workflows combining data access with LLM prompting.</p>
<p>The most popular example of context-augmentation is <a href="getting_started/concepts/">Retrieval-Augmented Generation or RAG</a>, which combines context with LLMs at inference time.</p>
<h3 id="what-are-agents">What are agents?<a class="headerlink" href="#what-are-agents" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p><a href="./understanding/agent/basic_agent/">Agents</a> are LLM-powered knowledge assistants that use tools to perform tasks like research, data extraction, and more. Agents range from simple question-answering to being able to sense, decide and take actions in order to complete tasks.</p>
<p>LlamaIndex provides a framework for building agents including the ability to use RAG pipelines as one of many tools to complete a task.</p>
<h3 id="what-are-workflows">What are workflows?<a class="headerlink" href="#what-are-workflows" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p><a href="./understanding/workflows/">Workflows</a> are multi-step processes that combine one or more agents, data connectors, and other tools to complete a task. They are event-driven software that allows you to combine RAG data sources and multiple agents to create a complex application that can perform a wide variety of tasks with reflection, error-correction, and other hallmarks of advanced LLM applications. You can then <a href="./module_guides/workflow/deployment.md">deploy these agentic workflows</a> as production microservices.</p>
<h3 id="llamaindex-is-the-framework-for-context-augmented-llm-applications">LlamaIndex is the framework for Context-Augmented LLM Applications<a class="headerlink" href="#llamaindex-is-the-framework-for-context-augmented-llm-applications" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>LlamaIndex imposes no restriction on how you use LLMs. You can use LLMs as auto-complete, chatbots, agents, and more. It just makes using them easier. We provide tools like:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Data connectors</strong> ingest your existing data from their native source and format. These could be APIs, PDFs, SQL, and (much) more.</li>
<li><strong>Data indexes</strong> structure your data in intermediate representations that are easy and performant for LLMs to consume.</li>
<li><strong>Engines</strong> provide natural language access to your data. For example:<ul>
<li>Query engines are powerful interfaces for question-answering (e.g. a RAG flow).</li>
<li>Chat engines are conversational interfaces for multi-message, "back and forth" interactions with your data.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Agents</strong> are LLM-powered knowledge workers augmented by tools, from simple helper functions to API integrations and more.</li>
<li><strong>Observability/Evaluation</strong> integrations that enable you to rigorously experiment, evaluate, and monitor your app in a virtuous cycle.</li>
<li><strong>Workflows</strong> allow you to combine all of the above into an event-driven system far more flexible than other, graph-based approaches.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="use-cases">Use cases<a class="headerlink" href="#use-cases" title="Permanent link">#</a></h2>
<p>Some popular use cases for LlamaIndex and context augmentation in general include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="use_cases/q_and_a/">Question-Answering</a> (Retrieval-Augmented Generation aka RAG)</li>
<li><a href="use_cases/chatbots/">Chatbots</a></li>
<li><a href="use_cases/extraction/">Document Understanding and Data Extraction</a></li>
<li><a href="use_cases/agents/">Autonomous Agents</a> that can perform research and take actions</li>
<li><a href="use_cases/multimodal/">Multi-modal applications</a> that combine text, images, and other data types</li>
<li><a href="use_cases/fine_tuning/">Fine-tuning</a> models on data to improve performance</li>
</ul>
<p>Check out our <a href="use_cases/">use cases</a> documentation for more examples and links to tutorials.</p>
<h3 id="who-is-llamaindex-for">👨‍👩‍👧‍👦 Who is LlamaIndex for?<a class="headerlink" href="#who-is-llamaindex-for" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>LlamaIndex provides tools for beginners, advanced users, and everyone in between.</p>
<p>Our high-level API allows beginner users to use LlamaIndex to ingest and query their data in 5 lines of code.</p>
<p>For more complex applications, our lower-level APIs allow advanced users to customize and extend any module -- data connectors, indices, retrievers, query engines, and reranking modules -- to fit their needs.</p>
<h2 id="getting-started">Getting Started<a class="headerlink" href="#getting-started" title="Permanent link">#</a></h2>
<p>LlamaIndex is available in Python (these docs) and <a href="https://ts.llamaindex.ai/">Typescript</a>. If you're not sure where to start, we recommend reading <a href="getting_started/reading/">how to read these docs</a> which will point you to the right place based on your experience level.</p>
<h3 id="30-second-quickstart">30 second quickstart<a class="headerlink" href="#30-second-quickstart" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>Set an environment variable called <code>OPENAI_API_KEY</code> with an <a href="https://platform.openai.com/api-keys">OpenAI API key</a>. Install the Python library:</p>
<div class="highlight"><pre><span></span><code>pip<span class="w"> </span>install<span class="w"> </span>llama-index
</code></pre></div>
<p>Put some documents in a folder called <code>data</code>, then ask questions about them with our famous 5-line starter:</p>
<div class="highlight"><pre><span></span><code><span class="kn">from</span> <span class="nn">llama_index.core</span> <span class="kn">import</span> <span class="n">VectorStoreIndex</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">SimpleDirectoryReader</span>

<span class="n">documents</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">SimpleDirectoryReader</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">&quot;data&quot;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">load_data</span><span class="p">()</span>
<span class="n">index</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">VectorStoreIndex</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">from_documents</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">documents</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">query_engine</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">index</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">as_query_engine</span><span class="p">()</span>
<span class="n">response</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">query_engine</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">query</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">&quot;Some question about the data should go here&quot;</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">response</span><span class="p">)</span>
</code></pre></div>
<p>If any part of this trips you up, don't worry! Check out our more comprehensive starter tutorials using <a href="getting_started/starter_example/">remote APIs like OpenAI</a> or <a href="getting_started/starter_example_local/">any model that runs on your laptop</a>.</p>
<h2 id="llamacloud">LlamaCloud<a class="headerlink" href="#llamacloud" title="Permanent link">#</a></h2>
<p>If you're an enterprise developer, check out <a href="https://llamaindex.ai/enterprise"><strong>LlamaCloud</strong></a>. It is an end-to-end managed service for data parsing, ingestion, indexing, and retrieval, allowing you to get production-quality data for your production LLM application. It's available both hosted on our servers or as a self-hosted solution.</p>
<h3 id="llamaparse">LlamaParse<a class="headerlink" href="#llamaparse" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>LlamaParse is our state-of-the-art document parsing solution. It's available as part of LlamaCloud and also available as a self-serve API. You can <a href="https://cloud.llamaindex.ai/">sign up</a> and parse up to 1000 pages/day for free, or enter a credit card for unlimited parsing. <a href="https://llamaindex.ai/enterprise">Learn more</a>.</p>

<h3 id="contributing">Contributing<a class="headerlink" href="#contributing" title="Permanent link">#</a></h3>
<p>We are open-source and always welcome contributions to the project! Check out our <a href="CONTRIBUTING/">contributing guide</a> for full details on how to extend the core library or add an integration to a third party like an LLM, a vector store, an agent tool and more.</p>
<h2 id="llamaindex-ecosystem">LlamaIndex Ecosystem<a class="headerlink" href="#llamaindex-ecosystem" title="Permanent link">#</a></h2>
<p>There's more to the LlamaIndex universe! Check out some of our other projects:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://github.com/run-llama/llama_deploy">llama_deploy</a> | Deploy your agentic workflows as production microservices</li>
<li><a href="https://llamahub.ai">LlamaHub</a> | A large (and growing!) collection of custom data connectors</li>
<li><a href="https://secinsights.ai">SEC Insights</a> | A LlamaIndex-powered application for financial research</li>
<li><a href="https://www.npmjs.com/package/create-llama">create-llama</a> | A CLI tool to quickly scaffold LlamaIndex projects</li>
</ul>

Importing Libraries

from llama_index.core.node_parser import SentenceSplitter

documents = SimpleDirectoryReader(input_files=["Medical_Records.pdf"]).load_data()

They are crucial to enable proper healthcare service deliv-\nery. Well-managed medical records allow smooth functioning and reduce the \nchances of human error. They are indispensable for audit and essential for research. \nIn developing countries, where the majority of patients are poor and a significant \nproportion illiterate, they provide unambiguous insight into events that have trans-\npired in previous encounters.\nAn Italian study by Poscia et\xa0 al. [1] that aimed to investigate the correlation \nbetween the level of implementation of clinical governance dimensions and the \nquality of medical records along with the extent to which it could promote quality \nimprovement in the context of a large Teaching Hospital found clinical governance \ninfluences health care quality, even in terms of the quality of medical records. It \nreiterates that well-kept medical records may be considered a surrogate marker of \ngood clinical governance.\n45.6  What Is the\xa0Administrative Importance \nof\xa0Medical Records?\nThe use of medical records surpasses current clinical practice and gains even more \nvalue in posterity. They are indispensable to medico-legal and malpractice suits \nwhere they have equal standing in defence and incrimination of health care provid-\ners and institutes. It is the legal liability of health care institutions to keep and main-\ntain in standardized format indoor patient medical records for at least 3\xa0years in \nIndia. In the USA, it is 6\xa0years as per HIPPA (the Health Insurance Portability and \nAccountability Act), The Canadian Medical Protective Association recommends \n10\xa0 years though it varies from jurisdiction to jurisdiction; Similarly, England \nrequires retention up to 10\xa0 years after death and electronic records must not be \ndestroyed.\n45 Medical Records', mimetype='text/plain', start_char_idx=None, end_char_idx=None, text_template='{metadata_str}\n\n{content}', metadata_template='{key}: {value}', metadata_seperator='\n'),

They even provide the epidemiological data on which national \nhealth policy as well as health expenditure may be based.\n45.7  How Do Medical Records Facilitate Research and\xa0Audit?\nRecord keeping is integral to both Research and Audit. For research, whether retro-\nspective or prospective, meticulous record of patient’s demographic and clinical data \nis imperative. For meaningful retrospective research, only meticulously maintained \nclinical records may yield patterns that can help improve practice. For instance, to \nevaluate intra-operative parameters that may significantly contribute to leaks in pan-\ncreatico-jejunal anastomoses in a centre correlation can only be demonstrated if data \nsuch as the texture of the pancreas, size of its duct, size, and location of the lesion, \nvascular anatomy, anastomotic technique, size and type of suture used etc. are dili-\ngently documented. Similarly, the first step in Audit is reviewing one’s own practice \nwhich is almost entirely hinged ongoing through past records. Also, to complete the \naudit cycle with re-audit, any demonstrable change is contingent on that change \nreflecting in records. Reviewing mortality files in regular mortality meets can help \nidentify preventable deaths. Similarly, regular audits can help identify near misses. \nAll of these together contribute to evidence-based and improved clinical care.\nDigitalization of medical records has made Audit and Research significantly less \ncumbersome. Patient data is available a click away. Furthermore, maintaining data \non spreadsheets allows one to use filters to specify research parameters. Also, if \nconsidered at the onset and planned, they even improve data portability.\nMost national and international standards for maintaining and accrediting EMRs \ninclude a mandatory review of records.\n45.8  How Are Medical Records Maintained?\nMedical Records may be recorded both in an electronic or paper format. Most \nhealth care organizations tend to use a combination of both.\nPaper records are traditional and widely kept. The responsibility and account-\nability are clearly allocated with the roles of data entry operators, doctors, and staff \nnurses defined.\nThe single largest value of electronic medical records (EMR) is in promoting \ntransparency, followed by, perhaps immeasurable but definitely welcome, impact of \nlegibility.\nEMR directly improves retrievability and follow-up of patients.\nIndirectly electronic records promote improved clinical governance, mitigating \nnot only pilferage and fabrication but also human error.45.8   How Are Medical Records Maintained?', mimetype='text/plain', start_char_idx=None, end_char_idx=None, text_template='{metadata_str}\n\n{content}', metadata_template='{key}: {value}', metadata_seperator='\n'),

45.14.2  Maintenance
Once adopted, the aim is to inculcate it in daily routine practice so the process 
becomes continuous. Most important aspect to prevent fractures is to retrain as the 
department cycles with turnover of new personnel, especially residents. Datasets 
and processes pinned on the department notice board/duty room/ward are helpful. 
Accountability and review which may be in the form of regular audits also boost 
improved record keeping.
45.14.3  Application
The effort-intensive nature of meticulous record-keeping merits it contributes to 
patient care and improved clinical service as well be of benefit to health care 
professionals.
Maintaining detailed records of not only patient data, but also their laboratory 
investigations, imagining studies etc. can aid retrospective meaningful research as 
well as audit, especially into perceived errors or mortality and even help identify 
near misses. Increased adoption Health information systems and EMR has made 
this conveniently feasible as it facilitates linking across platforms (laboratory ser -
vices, radiology, pharmacy etc.)45.14  How Can One Maintain Records in a Department?

from neo4j import GraphDatabase
import PyPDF2

def extract_entities_from_pdf(file_path):
    # Placeholder function to simulate extracting entities and relationships from the PDF
    # In a real scenario, you would use an NLP library to parse and extract entities and relationships
    entities = entities = [
    "Medical_Records",
    "Administrative_Data",
    "Legal_Data",
    "Financial_Data",
    "Clinical_Data",
    "Inpatient_Records",
    "Outpatient_Records",
    "Electronic_Medical_Records",
    "Paper_Medical_Records",
    "Patient_Demographic_Data",
    "Patient_Clinical_Data",
    "Medico_Legal_Data",
    "Hospital_Information_System",
    "Health_Records",
    "Healthcare_Providers",
    "Patient_Information"
]

    relationships = [
        ("Medical_Records", "Administrative_Data"),
        ("Medical_Records", "Legal_Data"),
        ("Medical_Records", "Financial_Data"),
        ("Medical_Records", "Clinical_Data"),
        ("Clinical_Data", "Inpatient_Records"),
        ("Clinical_Data", "Outpatient_Records"),
        ("Inpatient_Records", "History_Sheet"),
        ("Inpatient_Records", "Progress_Sheets"),
        ("Inpatient_Records", "Operative_Notes"),
        ("Inpatient_Records", "Referrals"),
        ("Inpatient_Records", "Discharge_Summary"),
        ("Medical_Records", "Electronic_Medical_Records"),
        ("Medical_Records", "Paper_Records"),
        ("Electronic_Medical_Records", "Clinical_Governance"),
        ("Electronic_Medical_Records", "Reduced_Errors"),
        ("Electronic_Medical_Records", "Accuracy_in_Clinical_Documentation"),
        ("Disease_A", "Symptom_1"),
        ("Disease_A", "Symptom_2"),
        ("Disease_A", "Treatment_1"),
        ("Disease_B", "Symptom_1"),
        ("Disease_B", "Treatment_2")
    ]

    return entities, relationships

def load_medical_records_data(file_path):
    driver = GraphDatabase.driver(
        uri="bolt://localhost:7687",
        auth=("neo4j", "Keerthi@98")
    )
    session = driver.session()

    entities, relationships = extract_entities_from_pdf(file_path)

    # Create nodes
    for entity in entities:
        session.run(f"MERGE (e:{entity.replace(' ', '_')})")

    # Create relationships
    for rel in relationships:
        session.run(f"""
            MATCH (a:{rel[0].replace(' ', '_')}), (b:{rel[1].replace(' ', '_')})
            MERGE (a)-[:RELATED_TO]->(b)
        """)

    session.close()

# Specify the path to your PDF file
file_path = pdf_path
load_medical_records_data(file_path)

default_cypher = """
MATCH (s)-[r]->(t)
RETURN s, r, t
"""

def showGraph(cypher: str = default_cypher):
    driver = GraphDatabase.driver(
        uri="bolt://localhost:7687",
        auth=("neo4j", "password")
    )
    session = driver.session()
    result = session.run(cypher)
    graph = result.graph()
    widget = GraphWidget(graph=graph)
    widget.node_label_mapping = 'id'
    return widget

showGraph()
